  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_169ac7a7-a232-443a-b4f6-e74bc8e578e6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12652409087285096913"><b>"A line that should never be crossed is about to be breached.<br/><br/>It puts this entire castle in jeopardy—and the life of your friend."</b><br/><br/>From the throne of glass rules a king with a fist of iron and a soul as black as pitch. Assassin Celaena Sardothien won a brutal contest to become his Champion. Yet Celaena is far from loyal to the crown. She hides her secret vigilantly; she know</span>
  <span id="freeText12652409087285096913" style="display:none"><b>"A line that should never be crossed is about to be breached.<br /><br />It puts this entire castle in jeopardy—and the life of your friend."</b><br /><br />From the throne of glass rules a king with a fist of iron and a soul as black as pitch. Assassin Celaena Sardothien won a brutal contest to become his Champion. Yet Celaena is far from loyal to the crown. She hides her secret vigilantly; she knows that the man she serves is bent on evil.<br /><br />Keeping up the deadly charade becomes increasingly difficult when Celaena realizes she is not the only one seeking justice. As she tries to untangle the mysteries buried deep within the glass castle, her closest relationships suffer. It seems no one is above questioning her allegiances—not the Crown Prince Dorian; not Chaol, the Captain of the Guard; not even her best friend, Nehemia, a foreign princess with a rebel heart.<br /><br />Then one terrible night, the secrets they have all been keeping lead to an unspeakable tragedy. As Celaena's world shatters, she will be forced to give up the very thing most precious to her and decide once and for all where her true loyalties lie... and whom she is ultimately willing to fight for.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12652409087285096913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

So, in truth, I reckon it depends on maturity to read this series, because I found it hard to put down!!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Spoilers!!!!<br /><br />Yeah Celæna is actually the Aelin person who's heir to Terrasen. Yes she's fae ~ Great -grandmother was Mab, an old Fae queenish-person, h<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Spoilers!!!!<br /><br />Yeah Celæna is actually the Aelin person who's heir to Terrasen. Yes she's fae ~ Great -grandmother was Mab, an old Fae queenish-person, her aunt Maeve (Sister of Mab) is current Queen of Wendlyn. <br />There were hints through the Crown of Midnight about Aelin but only properly revealed at the end.<br />Hope this answer helps<br />Enjoy reading Heir of Fire! <br />(I'm just going to pick it up once I've finished this comment.)<br /><a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_706537621" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706537621" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/706537621?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer706537621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16244990450158849779"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434749ra/877855.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Shit seriously just went down.</b> Oh wow, where do I start with this sequel? I wasn't even sure I was going to read it when I recently finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_' title='Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Throne of Glass</a> and found it entertaining but a poor excuse for fantasy. You want to know what <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_' title='Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Crown of Midnight</a> felt like? It was like the author listened to every piece of criticism I could have thrown at the first book, listened to everything I loved and everything that irritated me... and then wrote a perfect kind of book. The kind I wanted the first on</span>
  <span id="freeText16244990450158849779" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434749ra/877855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Shit seriously just went down.</b> Oh wow, where do I start with this sequel? I wasn't even sure I was going to read it when I recently finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> and found it entertaining but a poor excuse for fantasy. You want to know what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a> felt like? It was like the author listened to every piece of criticism I could have thrown at the first book, listened to everything I loved and everything that irritated me... and then wrote a perfect kind of book. The kind I wanted the first one to be; the kind I hadn't dared to hope she might produce in this sequel. There was more action, more nastiness, more character development, more surprises, more complications, more sexy, no love triangle - all of this and a well-placed, never-saw-it-coming twist. Ms Maas, consider me impressed.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a> takes a huge step away from the tame romantic/bitchy drama of its predecessor and opens up a story that is a bigger, bloodier and meaner than I think many readers will be expecting. Celaena gets to fully explore all aspects of what it means to be an assassin in this book; she is tested constantly and you can see her growing and changing and learning as the story progresses. And this story is one tumultuous journey of extremely high ups and unbelievably low downs with Celaena taking relationships to all new levels and watching others fall apart. Old enemies resurface and we start to get a glimpse of just how big the picture Maas is painting for us actually is. <br><br>One of the strengths of this book is having no idea how it's going to end. You might think that's a given, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> introduced us to a plot that was fairly easy to see mapped out. We are told of the challenges Celaena must compete in and win, we know that's what the book is moving towards, and it isn't too much of a leap to assume that (one way or another) Celaena is going to emerge victorious. Not in this book. This book starts with a blank slate, any mysteries or troubles that are to come are completely unknown to us - so every turn the plot takes is a surprise and every surprise is thrilling. I can't wrap my head around just <i>how much better</i> this sequel is. Maas has already grown as a writer and storyteller, making me wonder what she can possibly have in store for us next.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380434749ra/877856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The characters are also so much better developed in this book. Maas is brave enough here to allow the main characters to make mistakes, do the wrong things and test our ability to like them. Well, I don't know about you, but the new dimensions to their personalities, their faults and weaknesses, only served to make me like them more. Dorian surprised me most of all. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>, Dorian feels like something of a plot tool, a pretty little obstacle to Celaena and Chaol's romance. The scenes with him felt like filler between the parts I was actually waiting for. But not in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a>! In this, Dorian emerges as an interesting character with secrets of his own; he makes sacrifices for the people he loves and his importance to the bigger story starts to become apparent. <br><br><b>In short?</b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a>... <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434749i/877857.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Romance, love triangle, pretty dresses, one-dimensional characters, little action... </b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17167166.Crown_of_Midnight__Throne_of_Glass___2_" title="Crown of Midnight (Throne of Glass, #2) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown of Midnight</a>... <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380434749i/877858.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Badassery, twists, nastiness, betrayal, more action, magic, secrets...</b><br><br>If you were so-so about the first one and considering *maybe* reading this, you have my thumbs up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16244990450158849779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2742106605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9736141315822918718">5/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/05/05/crown-of-midnight-throne-of-glass-2-by-sarah-j-maas/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605628541i/30390369._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='370' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><b>Chaol Westfall, a well-trained, muscular grown-ass man, Captain of the Royal Guard</b>: *gets all soft and smooshy in this book*<br/><br/><b>me</b>: *needs to wrap him in a blanket, feed him some good hot Romanian rice pudding with lemon and sour cherry jam and protect him from the rest of the world because he is that precious* <br/>-	Actual plans that I really think about considering in a very serious way<br/><br/><br/><br/>After reading the first book of the series, <i>
  <b>Throne of Glass</b>
</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9736141315822918718" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2019/05/05/crown-of-midnight-throne-of-glass-2-by-sarah-j-maas/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605628541i/30390369._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="370" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><b>Chaol Westfall, a well-trained, muscular grown-ass man, Captain of the Royal Guard</b>: *gets all soft and smooshy in this book*<br><br><b>me</b>: *needs to wrap him in a blanket, feed him some good hot Romanian rice pudding with lemon and sour cherry jam and protect him from the rest of the world because he is that precious* <br>-	Actual plans that I really think about considering in a very serious way<br><br><br><br>After reading the first book of the series, <i>
  <b>Throne of Glass</b>
</i>, I knew that I enjoy <i>
  <b>Crown of Midnight</b>
</i>, but I’d never anticipated I’d enjoy it <i>that much</i>. <br><br>I've decided to read this book in a teeny-tiny complicated period of my life: I've been categorized by my ophthalmologist (cuz yeah, I wear glasses and not one but <i>
  <b>two</b>
</i> pairs, one of them being for reading, cuz yeah, my blind arse doesn't see well enough) as a "are case" and my eyes are „smashed" because of too much reading and it's not normal. Sooo I've been put through an "a carrot a day" cure and also "only 30 minutes of reading" cure. Because of that, I was not able to actually read as much as I wanted. But this book is giving to me a dependence that I am totally approving of, made me read so super-humanly fast that I've managed to actually read enough in a day to accumulate the plot, the characters' stories and the magic happening in general in Sarah J. Maas’ world.<br><br><b>This book was better than the first book from the beginning</b>. I think it is so much easier to get into the second book of the series because you have the advantage of the first one. In some series, the second, third, fourth etc. books are not as good as the first one. But in this series, you can actually <i>sense</i> them getting better and better (or maybe this is only my opinion). So second book of the Throne of Glass series &gt; the first book (but don’t get me wrong, I <b>loved</b> the first book too).<br><br>It is useless to talk about the plot at this point already: it’s the second book, some covered plans are being made in order to wipe the fussy king from the surface of this world. Talks about rebel alliances and plans and talks about some long-lost heir of Terrasen’s throne, Aelin Ashryver Galathynius start pumping the air of the book. Some think they are just rumours; some believe in them because their lives depend on these rumours. But until the end of the book, everything becomes just a huge ball of energy that absorbs everything (including your soul) and in my opinion, this is so important. <br><br>Sarah J. Maas is, in my opinion, a genius mind. She makes us fall in love, she makes us sigh, get angry, cry, wanna die and so on. All these elements are important spices in the whole dish of a book. I don’t know about other people, every single person has a personal taste, but I really think that this whole series is based on a brilliant idea, also very good narrated, even though I’ve read only two books. <br><br>Now, talking about spice, even though I am actually kind of a bit (more) in love with Dorian, the Crown Prince of Adarlan, and I think he is the most charming and witty son of a wicked king I’ve encountered (since present moment) in any of my reads (remember that I am fairly new to YA Fantasy club) and I love his beautiful soul and the way he and Celaena work together, I cannot not be happy to see how the relationship between Celaena and Chaol Westfall, Captain on the Guard, grew. At least in this particular book, at this given moment. Even though some batshit happens and Celaena goes cuckoo bird. <br><br>Going back, this book, the second book out of seven, blew my mind, made me laugh, made me sigh, made me cry, made me mad. And it was fantastic. Totally worth every single second I’ve spent reading it. I loved it.<br><br>Also, Nehemia Ytger, thank you for existing, Queen!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557049668i/27460694.jpg" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/e8c05072-9163-4eef-a25a-8adadd660b22_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9736141315822918718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreea Pop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreea Pop" href="/user/show/4858513-andreea-pop">Andreea Pop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398330049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5737231694966797063"><b>UPDATE: REVIEW 5++ STARS</b><br/><br/>Holy mother of all Gods! I'm starstruck. This is what I'd like to call a gorgeous sequel. Dare I say it, it might even top <i>Throne of Glass</i>! <br/><br/><a href='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-J6j1GnK8F2k/UhsOvTKsXPI/AAAAAAAAMTw/Keva4eISzaI/s1600/celaena3.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='320' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681160.jpg' width='212' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><a href='http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fkZntUZjW6w/UhsOvYyQPyI/AAAAAAAAMTo/XIGePpWbXtU/s1600/celaena2.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='320' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681161.jpg' width='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Celaena Sardothien is doing her job as King's Champion, meaning she's killing people that stepped on the king's toes. And now she's got a new target: Archer Finn, former crush and friend from the time when she was within the Assassin’s Guild. Turns out, she's not killing her targets, but faking their deaths, so she's in a lot </span>
  <span id="freeText5737231694966797063" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: REVIEW 5++ STARS</b><br><br>Holy mother of all Gods! I'm starstruck. This is what I'd like to call a gorgeous sequel. Dare I say it, it might even top <i>Throne of Glass</i>! <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-J6j1GnK8F2k/UhsOvTKsXPI/AAAAAAAAMTw/Keva4eISzaI/s1600/celaena3.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681160.jpg" width="212" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-fkZntUZjW6w/UhsOvYyQPyI/AAAAAAAAMTo/XIGePpWbXtU/s1600/celaena2.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681161.jpg" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Celaena Sardothien is doing her job as King's Champion, meaning she's killing people that stepped on the king's toes. And now she's got a new target: Archer Finn, former crush and friend from the time when she was within the Assassin’s Guild. Turns out, she's not killing her targets, but faking their deaths, so she's in a lot of danger if someone discovers her secret. The stakes are higher now that Archer is a well-known figure in Rifthold and that he might be involved in a rebel group. To make events even more complicated, the half-Fae and long-dead Queen, Elena, is asking Celaena to find the source behind the King's power.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Everything in this world is magic. Thank you ever so kindly for stating the obvious.”</b>
</i><br><br>Celaena was a goddamn badass. I wouldn't mess with her in a thousand years. We finally see her wild and deadly side, the one that I've grown accustomed to in the prequel e-novellas and that wasn't fully explored in <i>Throne of Glass</i>. Sure, she's still that sassy, arrogant and sarcastic girl, but above all, she's an assassin. A ruthless killer. And when the ones she loves are in danger or threatened, she's unforgiving. That part of her really gives you goosebumps. Oh, and let's not forget when she's in for revenge. One word: lethal.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-B7M1VX6JX0w/UhsOvaku6BI/AAAAAAAAMTs/rTrJ83ryMiI/s1600/assassin.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681162.jpg" width="214" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>She was a whirlwind of steel and blood. As he watched her cut through the men like they were stalks of wheat in a field, he understood how she had gotten so close to touching Endovier’s wall that day. And at last—after all these months—he saw the lethal predator he’d expected to find in the mines. There was nothing human in her eyes, nothing remotely merciful. It froze his heart.</b>
</i><br><br>Dorian Havilliard. Chaol Westfall. Dorian, Chaol, Chaol, Dorian. Chaol is the same sweet, loyal, funny, protective and fierce warrior. I loved his easy banter with Celaena and his alpha-male demeanor. Prince Dorian Havilliard is still the same passionate, kind, intelligent young man that is slowly transforming into a great ruler. And they’re best friends! How can I choose?! <i>*crying*</i><br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-cNV-tiUFXrE/UhsOyrxyz6I/AAAAAAAAMT8/ZuDhUFQu_wg/s1600/dorian.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681163.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-RUhJLAXPkXc/UhsOzygMX1I/AAAAAAAAMUE/e-bPlpdtEic/s1600/chaol.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681164.jpg" width="270" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“I worry because I care. Gods help me, I know I shouldn't, but I do. So I will always tell you to be careful, because I will always care what happens.”</b>
</i><br><br>In <i>Crown of Midnight</i>, Chaol and Celaena are getting close. Like really close. And because of that, both of their relationships with Dorian become more strained, awkward and tense. And that's kind of the single thing that bothered me at Celaena: in <i>Throne of Glass</i>, she was all over Dorian... and now? She doesn't care about his feelings when he clearly loves her. And that just got me going mad. I wanted to hug Dorian several times and give him cookies. <br><br>Still, things evolve a little bit between them on a platonic level when a heartbreaking twist makes Celaena not trust Chaol anymore. And another unexpected twist involving Dorian makes things one hundred times more interesting. <br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-oJhplVdCW0o/UhsPB8x2h5I/AAAAAAAAMUc/ByX4Gl9Wtbg/s1600/tumblr_inline_mlktodx8sD1qz4rgp.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="160" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681165.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>“When you do, I want you to remember that it wouldn’t have made any difference to me. It’s never made any difference to me when it came to you. I’d still pick you. I’ll always pick you.”</b>
</i><br><br>I've read some reviews that say that the love triangle's fate is sealed after the first quarter of the book. But now, after reading it, I'm not so sure. Especially after that second half and killer ending. I love Chaol with all my heart, but I can't help but hope that Celaena will end up with Dorian. Now, now, don't throw stones at me! It’s still a <i>Cinderella</i> inspired book! They're both swoony guys, but I've always loved Dorian a bit more. Might be because of the dark-haired, blue-eyed appearance. And possibly the arrogance. And the bookish and funny personality. Perhaps even the fact that he's a freaking prince. <i>*dreamy sigh*</i><br><br><i>
  <b>“If you are captured, if you are hurt, you are beyond our reach. You will be entirely on your own.”<br>“I’ll be fine.”<br>“But I won’t be. Every day that you’re there, I will wonder what has become of you. I won’t.... I won’t forget you. Not for one hour.”</b>
</i><br><br>Nehemia was such a great support for Celaena, even if she had her own agenda. The princess is one of those selfless characters that would give everything up for the sake of her people. She's fair, ambitious and dedicated. And she's the key-player that sets things in motion in this sequel. But in a gut-wrenching method that will surely have you shedding a few tears.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-dVn4UjgnHBs/UhsO3EeV5XI/AAAAAAAAMUM/nIE5nvljTrw/s1600/nahemia.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681166.jpg" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The villain we love to hate: the King of Adarlan, Dorian's father. His plans turn out to be down-right evil and unnatural. I loathe that guy because he's so willing to exploit everyone around him for his own sake. I want him <b>D.E.A.D.</b> <i>*guilty smile*</i><br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Kkh_05pFsmE/UhsPKvMyDhI/AAAAAAAAMUk/nba22hAusHk/s1600/tumblr_moh59oPqcS1r2fqvso1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681167.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>As it was to be expected, we meet new characters. My favorite was Mort. Why? First of all, he's an ancient <i>
  <b>talking</b>
</i> door knocker. Second of all, he's hilarious! <br><br><i>
  <b>When they left, Nehemia spent a few minutes studying Mort— mostly asking him questions about his creation spell, which he claimed to have forgotten, then claimed was too private, then claimed she had no business hearing.</b>
</i><br><br>Archer Finn was hard to read, but I never trusted him behind all those pretty smiles and coward-like behavior. Never trust a courtesan. Oh, and of course, there's Baba Yellowlegs. Even the name gives you creeps. She's an old, manipulative witch whose favorite meal is consisted of young girls. Told you: creepy. <br><br>The character development is really spectacular. You can see how Celaena, Chaol and Dorian grow. By the end of the novel, our heroine is not running from her past anymore; the Captain of the Guard is ready to sacrifice himself and face his father; and the Crown Prince starts to stand up to the King no matter the consequences.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-N7v9XfoPNRI/UhsO4rYYBXI/AAAAAAAAMUU/ACn-fF7WSXk/s1600/warrior.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681168.jpg" width="228" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br><i>
  <b>“Thank you for all that you have done for me, Dorian. Thank you for being my friend. For not being like the others.”</b>
</i><br><br>The pace was definitely action driven. I'm not kidding when I'm saying that sooo much happened and some many plots started to unfold between my eyes. Crown of Midnight was a page-turner through and through and there was never a dull moment.<br> <br><i>
  <b>“How long will you keep her here?” Dorian said, looking down the stairs.<br>She had attacked the Captain of the Guard in front of his men. Worse than attacked.<br>“As long as it takes,” Chaol said quietly.<br>"For what?”<br>“For her to decide not to kill us all.”</b>
</i><br><br>Another think that surprised me was the fact that Celaena is keeping so many secrets I can't even keep count. There were two revelations regarding her: I suspected the one revealed in the end, but the other one totally caught me unprepared. Both are jaw-dropping twists that will completely change the outcome of her adventures.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I’ll come back,” she said quietly. “I’ll come back for you.”</b>
</i><br><br>The world-building was exquisite! We learn so much more about Erilea, Adarlan and the history of the country. We delve deeper into the Fae magic. It's a top-notch high fantasy world, coupled with a darker atmosphere, mistery, magic and amazing characters. The result is a certain recipe for epicness, one that Sarah J. Mass gorgeously created with her mad writing skills. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-gGce_P-8eVE/UhsOwVd4RDI/AAAAAAAAMT4/ktPWfdrk0wU/s1600/stag.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="284" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226544i/681169.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you haven't started this series, I'm begging you -- pick it up <b>ASAP</b>. It's complex, emotional and completely captivating. You'll laugh, you'll cry, you'll swoon, you'll gasp in shock and you'll fall in love with the story. <i>Crown of Midnight</i> was an excellent follow-up that might not end in a claw-your-yes-out sort of cliffhanger, but it will make you crave the next installment like air. And man, what a ride that will be! <i>*wink*</i><br><br><b>ENJOY!&lt;3<br><br><i>You can also read this review here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://raftul-cartilor-vampiresti.blogspot.ro/2013/08/review-crown-of-midnight-throne-of.html">http://raftul-cartilor-vampiresti.blo...</a><br><br>..........................................<br><br><b>I NEED THIS BOOK!!!</b> How can I wait another year?? It's killing me!!!!<br><br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-b2SBeHoEw2c/UDX1WHdTToI/AAAAAAAAEGo/h2uPp5WS01c/s1600/tumblr_m7jblg26qB1rbfthno1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681170.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br></i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5737231694966797063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <b>5 BILLION STARS</b>
  </i>
</p><br><br><br><p>
  <i>Don't get me started on <i>the cover</i>,because you all know how much I appreciate these beauties.This series has everything on it's perfection,starting from the covers to the story and the characters,and everything.Simply perfection.</i>

  <b>
    <i>“Who said anything about shame?" She gestured down to her naked body, even though it was covered by the blanket. "Honestly, I'm surprised you're not strutting about, boasting to everyone. I certainly would be if I'd tumbled me.<br>"Does your love for yourself know no bounds?"<br>"Absolutely none.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><p><i>Throne of Glass</i> was a 5 star book for me,but comparing to this one,I don't know,this stands out in every single way.This is probably the best book I have read so far this year.I knew I will freaking love it from the first page.The story is more developed,the characters are too,and there's a moment where everything changes.That mind blowing moment that you should read to understand it,to live it.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426701056i/14082721._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What does that mean?" he demanded.<br>She smiled sadly. "You'll figure it out. And when you do..." She shook her head, knowing she shouldn't say it, but doing it anyway. "When you do, I want you to remember that it wouldn't have made any difference to me. It's never made any difference to me when it came to you. I’d still pick you. I’ll always pick you.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><p><i>The story</i> follow Celaena,now officially the king's champion,doing his dirty work.The king sends her to kill people but she fakes every death.This trick becomes harder day by day,because she puts in risk the people she loves,her friends,her freedom and her being.She is torn between two protectors,Chaol and Dorian,who fight for her in different ways.But there comes a darker force,which Celaena has to fight,because it is her destiny,even if you wants or not.</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426701056i/14082722.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Why are you crying?"<br>"Because," she whispered, her voice shaking, "you remind me of what the world ought to be. What the world can be.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><p>If you remember my review of Throne of Glass,you would know that I did not loved Celaena,especially at the beginning,but gosh,she is now of my favorite characters I have ever read about.She is strong,and loyal and beautiful and has that weird sense of humor,that I truly dig,what can I say,I am in love:)</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426701056i/14082723.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The rest of the world quieted into nothing. In that moment, after ten long years, Celaena looked at Chaol and realised she was home.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><p>My favorite part was when Archer kidnapped Chaol and Celaena went to save him.That entry in the warehouse was phenomenal and so bad ass.</p><br><br><p>
  <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
    <i>Rest in peace Nehemia :( </i>
   <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426701056i/14082724._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I worry because I care. Gods help me, I know I shouldn't, but I do. So I will always tell you to be careful, because I will always care what happens.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>____________________________________________<br><br><br><p>I <i>highly</i> recommend this book if you have read Throne of Glass already.If you haven't then go check it out first and come to this one,because this book is perfection,like literally perfection.</p><br><br>*Pictures from the review are not mine, I took them mostly from Google images or Tumblr*</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2365385106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365385106" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365385106?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365385106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12439548617964903225">Celaena may be many things but she is <b>
  <i>not a murderer. </i>
</b><br/><br/>She is an <b>
  <i>assassin.</i>
</b><br/><br/> There's a difference. (Probably.) <blockquote>
  <i>He had no idea what sort of darkness lurked inside her, or what sort of monster she was willing to become in order to make things right.</i>
</blockquote> I honestly don't even know where to start with this one. It was so good and I'm just absolutely reeling from that ending. Because. Wow.<b> Sarah J. Maas just delivered on this sequel.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Enough! We have enough enemies as it is! There are worse th</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12439548617964903225" style="display:none">Celaena may be many things but she is <b>
  <i>not a murderer. </i>
</b><br /><br />She is an <b>
  <i>assassin.</i>
</b><br /><br /> There's a difference. (Probably.) <blockquote>
  <i>He had no idea what sort of darkness lurked inside her, or what sort of monster she was willing to become in order to make things right.</i>
</blockquote> I honestly don't even know where to start with this one. It was so good and I'm just absolutely reeling from that ending. Because. Wow.<b> Sarah J. Maas just delivered on this sequel.</b><blockquote>
  <i>"Enough! We have enough enemies as it is! There are worse things out there to face!"<br /><br />Celaena slowly turned to him, her face splattered with blood and eyes blazing bright. "No, there aren't," she said. "Because I'm here now."</i>
</blockquote> Celaena Sardothien ex-prisoner of the salt mines has risen to the position of<b> Royal Assassin. </b> She must follow every whim of her king for four years. Only then, will she <b>finally be freed.</b><br /><br />It was a hard bargain but Celaena <b>thought she could handle it. </b>She's killed many, many before - so how could killing for the King be any different?<br /><br />The Mad (or merely cruel?) King sees spies and traitors everywhere. He frequently sends her out to murder innocents. To murder - <b>not to assassinate</b> - and that makes all the difference.<br /><br />Very quickly Celaena finds ways to smuggle out these would-be-victims, but with the ever-rising number of "survivors" (any one of them could blow her cover), the ever-increasing threat from home and the reappearance of an old <s>friend</s> -<b> how could she even hope to protect those who matter to her most?</b><br /><br />I absolutely love how our main character is <b>confident, beautiful and completely in control </b>- it's such a refreshing change from all the awkward, please-tell-me-I'm-pretty and helpless heroines that populate many YA books.<blockquote>
  <i> If they wanted Adarlan's Assassin, they'd get her. <br />And Wyrd help them when she arrived.</i>
</blockquote> The side-characters are so well-done. There's a bit of a love-triangle. Normally, I'd run away screaming at the hint of a love triangle (I've suffered through so many terrible ones) but Sarah J. Maas executed it perfectly. (<i>Is there anything that the Maas-ter can't do?</i>)<br /><br /> Plus, that ending just <b>sucked out my last breath.</b>It was such a twist and it was so incredibly badass. I loved it. <blockquote>
  <i>Death was her curse and her gift, and death had been her good friend these long, long years.</i>
</blockquote><b> If you haven't picked up this series yet - get it today. Seriously. Go. Now.</b><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_2047881674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047881674" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047881674?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781408834947" href="/book/show/17670709-crown-of-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047881674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1049961203067929181"><i>“Some things you hear with your ears. Others, you hear with your heart.”</i><br/><br/>To say Sarah J. Maas stepped up her game in the second book of her <b>“Throne of Glass Series”</b> most certainly would be the understatement of the century. No, scratch that, it actually doesn’t even get close to the truth. XD<br/><br/>I swear in comparison to the first book this truly was an action packed and suspenseful read! =)<br/>Alone the many awesome fight scenes and the countless revelations throughout the entire book were already enough</span>
  <span id="freeText1049961203067929181" style="display:none"><i>“Some things you hear with your ears. Others, you hear with your heart.”</i><br /><br />To say Sarah J. Maas stepped up her game in the second book of her <b>“Throne of Glass Series”</b> most certainly would be the understatement of the century. No, scratch that, it actually doesn’t even get close to the truth. XD<br /><br />I swear in comparison to the first book this truly was an action packed and suspenseful read! =)<br />Alone the many awesome fight scenes and the countless revelations throughout the entire book were already enough to cause my head to spin! Plus Celaena finally lives up to her reputation as Adarlan’s best assassin and actually kills people, which was amazing and involuntarily made me love this even more! *lol* <br /><br />Yes, Sarah can write and her action scenes always had me at the edge of my seat. Once or twice I might have even been close to falling off of my chair, but that’s another matter for another day! ;-P<br />For now all you have to know is that <b>”Crown of Midnight”</b> was an awesome read and that it was able to keep me on my toes and considering how many books I already read, this certainly should speak for itself. ;-)<br /><br />Since I don’t really feel like talking about <b>the plot</b> (you’ll read plenty of it in my characters section aka The Spoilery Spoiler Section anyway) I’ll do something completely mean and will only give you a few words:<br />Celaena, Chaol, Dorian, The King, Roland, Kaltain, Nehemia, Archer, missions, blood, death, creepy, magic, dungeons, books and let’s not forget about Fleetfoot! <br /><br />There you go! *lol* Haha! Oh Jeez that’s so vague you’ll hate me! XD<br /><br />Well, anyway! *smiles innocently*<br />Let’s get to my favourite section! <br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Do I still have to say it?! Yes? Okay! This is the aforementioned “Spoilery Spoiler Part” so if you don’t want to read quotes or spoilers or my crazy thoughts, you better stop now and never return. ;-P Don’t say I didn’t warn you!</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Celaena:</b><br /><br /><i>”Some days, it feels like another person did those things. And most of those lives I’m glad I ended. No matter the cause, though, it – it still takes away a little piece of you each time. So I don’t think I’ll ever forget them.”</i><br /><br />Celaena is so kick-ass, I love her!!! We finally saw the relentless killer in her and I just couldn’t get enough of it! I thoroughly enjoyed all of the fighting scenes and the one with Baba Yellowlegs was definitely the best! XD I can’t wait to read more about those Ironteeth Witch Clans and I really hope they’ll be a part of the other books! Aside from the action I probably enjoyed Celaena’s character development the most. She’s no longer afraid to show her true self and she doesn’t only open up to Chaol but also to Dorian. I can’t say how much I loved all those new revelations about her and the fact that she’s fae took me entirely by surprise. I definitely didn’t expect that and I was like <b>“WOAH WHAT?!!!”</b> when I read it! I mean I always knew she had a secret and Sarah mentioned it often enough, I certainly didn’t expect it to be this kind of secret though!! *lol* I’m sure after the promise at Nehemia’s grave we can expect great things in the future and I’m so curious about Wendlyn; I immediately want to start with <b>“Heir of Fire”.</b><br /><br /><i>”I failed him,” she said. “In every way that counted, I failed him.”<br />Another long silence, then a sigh. “Not in one way.” Chaol said. “I bet he would have wanted you to survive – to live. So you didn’t fail him, not in that regard.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I want you to know,” she whispered to the wind, to the earth, to the body far beneath her, “that you were right. You were right. I am a coward. And I have been running for so long that I’ve forgotten what it is to stand and fight.”</i><br /><br /><i>”The ship began moving. And Chaol – the man she hated and loved so much that she could hardly think around him – just stood there, watching her go.”</i><br /><br /><b>Chaol:</b><br /><br /><i>”She was a whirlwind of steel and blood. As he watched her cut through the men as though they were stalks of wheat in a field, he understood how she had gotten so close to touching Endovier’s wall that day. And at last – after all these months – he saw the lethal predator he’d expected to find in the mines. There was nothing human in her eyes, nothing remotely merciful. It froze his heart.”</i><br /><br />Ahh Chaol! My problem child! *sighs* I don’t hate him, actually I like him, but <b>ARGH!!!!</b> He screwed up big time in this one and I just couldn’t believe what I read! I mean come on! You’re the Captain of the King’s Guard! You should be smarter than that!!! Seriously, in this book I really began to hate his loyalty to the king and it made me more than just angry that he never even thought about questioning the king’s orders! Chaol basically is the embodiment of the unthinking and unblinking soldier! Stupidly loyal to a fault!!! And that moment when he got kidnapped in his own domain? <b>
  <u>WHAT THE FREAKEDY FREAKING HELL?!</u>
</b> Like: Are you kidding me!? I can’t help but wonder how he even became the Captain of the Guard. *lol* I’m so not impressed. Not at all! Plus he should have told Celaena about Nehemia, but he didn’t and that once again tells me that he still doesn’t trust her. At the end I felt kind of sad for him though. I mean he finally realised that he was blind and probably made the biggest mistake of his life. Unfortunately by then it was already too late to change anything about his misguided actions and he ended up suffering like crazy. Poor Chaol! =(<br /><br /><i>”Once, Chaol might have argued. Once, he might have protested that his loyalty to the crown was his greatest asset. But that blind loyalty and obedience had started his descent.<br />And it had destroyed everything.</i><br /><br /><i>”But when Celaena walked out, leaving that damning will behind him, he didn’t even make it to his own room. He barely made it into an empty broom closet before the sobs hit.”</i><br /><br /><i>”But he could do this for her. Even if he never saw her again, even if she abandoned her duties as King’s Champion and stayed with the Fae in Wendlyn forever – as long as he knew that she was safe, that no one could hurt her … He’d sell his soul again and again for that.”</i><br /><br /><b>Dorian:</b><br /><br /><i>”You have power in you, Prince. More power than you realize.” She touched his chest, tracing a symbol there, too, and some of the court ladies gasped. But Nehemia’s eyes were locked on his. “It sleeps,” she whispered, tapping his heart. “In here. When the time comes, when it awakens, do not be afraid.” She removed her hand and gave him a sad smile. “When it is time, I will help you.”</i><br /><br /><u>
  <b>My charming and precious cutiepie!!!</b>
</u> I love Dorian so damn much! He’s the best thing about the entire series and in <b>“Crown of Midnight”</b> he broke my heart. I suffered with him throughout the entire book and I really hate the idea that Sarah might make him a second Lucien. Neither of those two boys deserved what she put them through and I really hope she won’t continue to harm him in the next book. He’s just too pure for the world and he needs to be protected at all costs!!! Plus he’s amazing!!! <br /><br />I love the fact that he has raw magic in him and I see so much potential for the next few books! Still, his loneliness caused my heart to ache and I felt really sorry for him. He’s so alone and no one is there to help him, yet his first thought when he discovered that he had magic was that he needs to find out if his brother has it too. He wanted to protect Hollin and that’s so damn sweet! &lt;33 Oh boy, how much I wanted to hug him when he frantically tried to hide his research in the library or when he was looking for Nehemia and waited in front of Celaena’s rooms. All this anger and despair - He doesn’t deserve it!!! Sarah, please have mercy on him!!!<br /><b>#TeamDorian forever and for always!!!!</b><br /><br /><i>”How long have you been yearning for him? Was what he really wanted to ask. Damn him for caring. Damn him for every moment he’d spent with her.”</i><br /><br /><i>”How about you spend a year in Calaculla, and when you’re done, you two can sit here and tell me about your plans for expansion.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Something invisible slammed into the creature, sending it flying into the wall with a crunch. Gods. Dorian didn’t just have magic – he had raw magic. The rarest, and deadliest, kind. Sheer undiluted power, capable of being shaped into whatever form the wielder desired.”</i><br /><br /><b>Nehemia:</b><br /><br /><i>”I won’t deny that you have suffered, Elentiya, but there are thousands more who have also suffered – and suffered more. And they do not sell themselves to the king to get what they, too, deserve. With each person you kill, I am finding fever and fewer excuses for remaining your friend.”</i><br /><br /><b>WHY SARAH!!!??</b> Why did you have to kill Nehemia? She was such a lovely character and I didn’t expect her death! When Celaena found out about the King’s intentions I really thought that she’d be able to safe her or would at least come just in time to exchange some final words with her. But no! We found a dead Nehemia and Celaena never got a chance to fix things between them. T_T I hate it that they had an argument before she died and I really don’t like the way Nehemia had to die. I mean she didn’t even get a fighting scene. We’re presented with a fait accompli, which sucked! Well, at least in my opinion. So there’s that! Can’t say I feel sorry for Grave or Archer though. They had it coming and they should have known better than to mess with Celaena. *lol*<br /><br /><i>”I have grown up knowing the weight of my crown. When the king invaded Eyllwe all those years ago, I knew that I would someday have to make choices that would haunt me.” She cupped her forehead in a palm. “I didn’t think it would be this hard. I cannot be in two places at once.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Nehemia was gone. That vibrant, fierce, loving soul; the princess who had been called the Light of Eyllwe; the woman who had been a beacon of hope – just like that, as if she were no more than a wisp of candlelight, she was gone.”</i><br /><br /><i>”But no matter what I did, Elentiya, I want you to know that in the darkness of the past ten years, you were one of the bright lights for me. Do not let that light go out.”</i><br /><br /><b>Kaltain and Roland:</b><br /><br /><i>”Sometimes,” Kaltain said softly, and Celaena paused. “Sometimes I think they brought me here. Not to marry Perrington, but for another purpose. They want to use me.”</i><br /><br />I still don’t know what the king plans with Kaltain and Roland but whatever it is, it can’t be good! That thing in the dungeons underneath the clock tower was so creepy and I really don’t even want to know what else is locked up there! *shudders* There’s no doubt the King of Adarlan is up to something and I’m kind of worried about Kaltain’s fate. I have no idea where and how Roland comes into play, but I get the slight feeling he’s allied with the king. I mean yeah he helped Dorian but maybe that was all show? Who knows? I’ll definitely watch those two closely from now on. ;-)<br /><br /><i>"They encourage the crows to fly past here," Kaltain murmured, more to herself than to Celaena. "And my headaches are worse every day. Worse and worse, and full of all those flapping wings."</i><br /><br /><b>The friendships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Celaena &amp; Dorian:</u><br /><br /><i>”She deserved a loyal, brave knight who saw her for what she was and did not fear her. And he deserved someone who would look at him like that, even if the love wouldn’t be the same, even if the girl wouldn’t be her.<br />So Dorian closed his eyes, and took another long breath. And when he opened his eyes, he let her go.”</i><br /><br /><b>Those two!!!</b> I know they had troubles at the beginning but the friendship that formed between them is so perfect!!! I’m so happy that they were able to settle their differences and I love Dorian for letting her go! This was such a powerful scene and I’m so glad they eventually managed to become friends again! I loved it when Dorian told Celaena that she will always have a place with him and that she could come to his dorms whenever she needed something. <b>THAT</b> is friendship!!! <b>THAT</b> is trust!!! Oh gosh, I really hope Sarah won’t crush this again! *lol* <br /><br /><i>”Their eyes met and held. A line stretched taut between them – a moment of trust, and a promise of answers from both of them.”</i><br /><br /><i>”But looking at Dorian as he smiled at her, this prince who was smart and thoughtful and kind, who inspired good men like Chaol to serve him … <br />Celaena wondered if Nehemia’s impossible, desperate dream of that court might yet come to pass.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Thank you for all that you have done for me, Dorian. Thank you for being my friend. For not being like the others.” He paused, turning to face her. She kept her chin high, but her eyes were gleaming.<br />“I’ll come back,” she said quietly. “I’ll come back for you.”</i><br /><br /><u>Dorian &amp; Chaol:</u><br /><br /><i>Dorian’s lips were pursed, his face stony as he quietly said, “I’ve been busy, too.” The Crown Prince turned his horse away, heading in another direction, but paused. “Chaol,” he said, looking over his shoulder. Dorian’s eyes were frozen, his jaw clenched. “Treat her well.”</i><br /><br />*sigh* Their friendship suffered so much in this book and I really wish this wouldn’t have happened. I loved that they were so close and could talk about everything, but I guess now that Celaena got into their way things between them might never be the same again. &gt;_&lt; It’s sad that Dorian can’t tell Chaol about his powers but I definitely understand why he’s so cautious. I mean Chaol was always so damn loyal to the king and that actually makes it more than just hard to trust him. If I’d be in Dorian’s situation, I wouldn’t tell him as well. =( <br /><br /><i>”Dorian could have gleefully killed Chaol’s father for disowning him, refusing even to see Chaol when he brought his family to Rifthold for an important meeting with the king. Even though Chaol had never said it, Dorian knew the scars went deep.”</i><br /><br /><u>Celaena &amp; Chaol:</u><br /><br /><i>”I know you can look after yourself. But I worry because I care. Gods help me, I know I shouldn’t, but I do. So I will always tell you to be careful, because I will always care what happens.”</i><br /><br />I can’t believe Sarah used 1 ½ books to build this relationship and then decided to thoroughly sink the ship! Oh wait! I actually <b>
  <u>CAN</u>
</b> believe it! *LOL* After reading ACOTAR nothing should surprise me anymore! Still, I mean I never was the biggest fan of this ship (everyone who read my review of ToG knows that) but I at least would have wanted them to be happy for a while. And the way it happened!! <br /><br />I can understand that Celaena was angry at Chaol but I really didn’t get why she acted the way she did. I mean at first she’s all in love with Chaol and jumps to his rescue because he’s been kidnapped and all she wants is to save him because <b>she loves him oh so much</b> and then in the next moment she’s at his throat and almost kills him! Hell! She didn’t even give him a chance to explain himself! Yes, I’m aware this would have changed nothing about Nehemia’s death, but I think if she would have let him talk, she’d have realised that he didn’t know about the king’s plans. She wronged poor Chaol so much and even though he made bad decisions I still feel sorry for him. Because let’s face it, he might have never trusted Celaena but he certainly loved her deeply. T_T <br /><b>What a shipwreck!!!</b> RIP!<br /><br /><i>”She knew his every move and he knew hers, as though they’d been dancing this waltz together all their lives. Faster, never faltering, never breaking her stare.<br />The rest of the world quieted into nothing. In that moment, after ten long years, Celaena looked at Chaol and realized she was home.”</i><br /><br /><i>”It had snuck up on him, this pain and terror and rage at the thought of anyone else with her. Every look, every word from her … He didn’t even know when it had started.”</i><br /><br /><i>”But he didn’t know how to get her in line. He didn’t know how to fix what had been broken. Both inside her, and between them.”</i><br /><br />All told I really loved <b>“Crown of Midnight”</b> and I can’t wait to dive into <b>“Heir of Fire.”</b> Since this was another buddy read with my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49958029-gemma-bunksmccoy" rel="nofollow noopener">precious Gem</a> I actually enjoyed the experience even more! XD I loved our discussions about the plot and characters and the fact Gem is such a hardcore Chaol fan only added <s>fire to the fuel</s> to the fun. *lol* <br /><br />Let’s pick up book 3 soon!!! I promise I won’t talk bad about Chaol! Well, I’ll try not to! Scout’s honor! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="1049961203067929181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2348352024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10674395153810648146">upon reread, ive decided to bump up my rating. knowing how the story plays out over the span of 7 books, its allowed me to view this with a different perspective. when i first read this, i didnt like how much page-time is focused on boring history, but now i can really appreciate all of the top-notch foreshadowing thats going on. <br/><br/>everything else in my original review still applies. <br/><br/>___________________________<br/><br/>firstly, wow! i think this might be better than the first book! and i actually really li</span>
  <span id="freeText10674395153810648146" style="display:none">upon reread, ive decided to bump up my rating. knowing how the story plays out over the span of 7 books, its allowed me to view this with a different perspective. when i first read this, i didnt like how much page-time is focused on boring history, but now i can really appreciate all of the top-notch foreshadowing thats going on. <br /><br />everything else in my original review still applies. <br /><br />___________________________<br /><br />firstly, wow! i think this might be better than the first book! and i actually really liked <i>'throne of glass,'</i> so thats saying something!<br /><br />secondly, i saw a status update the other day where someone expressed their frustration with how women in novels, specifically YA, are too often portrayed as fierce and dangerous. while i agree that kindness and gentleness should also be represented, i have to say that i <i>live</i> for my ruthless and downright deadly ladies. <br /><br />for me, reading about celaena, about an assassin, is insight into a world i would never experience in a million years. i dont have a violent bone in my body. i actually think my body is programmed with a ‘flight and flight’ response. so i love being able to experience what its like for someone to have so much conviction that she would literally kill for what she believed in. that is the beauty of books, my friends. <br /><br />so give me a merciless assassin any day of the week. you go, girl! see ya in book #3! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_424844368" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/424844368" />
    <a title="mara • (chaotic reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader"><img alt="mara • (chaotic reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493058074p2/12902362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/424844368?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mara • (chaotic reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mara • (chaotic reader)" href="/user/show/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader">mara • (chaotic reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18846563-crown-of-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader?shelf=fae-and-otherworldly-beings">fae-and-otherworldly-beings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12902362-mara-chaotic-reader?shelf=assassins-and-spies">assassins-and-spies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer424844368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17695261526658553875"><b>4.5 stars</b> <br/><i>Hear ye, hear ye all who seek adventure, ass-kicking and romance come forth! The second installment doth not disappoint! Our heroine is back as the King's Champion so expect action galore. Hear ye, hear ye . . .</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Her lovely dresses and ornate clothes were gone, replaced with an unforgiving, close-cut black tunic and pants. Her hair pulled back in a long braid that fell into the folds of that dark cloak she was always wearing. She was a beautiful wrath …</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book turned up in </span>
  <span id="freeText17695261526658553875" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> <br><i>Hear ye, hear ye all who seek adventure, ass-kicking and romance come forth! The second installment doth not disappoint! Our heroine is back as the King's Champion so expect action galore. Hear ye, hear ye . . .</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Her lovely dresses and ornate clothes were gone, replaced with an unforgiving, close-cut black tunic and pants. Her hair pulled back in a long braid that fell into the folds of that dark cloak she was always wearing. She was a beautiful wrath …</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book turned up in my room dressed in dark robes, whispered the first few sentences like a secret incantation and before I could utter <i>'By the Wyrd'</i> I was under its spell (not saying that this book has magical powers, but this book has magical powers . . . in fact I'm pretty sure Sarah J. Maas is Fae). It swept me down a path of ink and words, and every time I thought it had given me its all, <i>'surely it can't get better than this . . . surely,'</i> it would open its robes to unveil yet more wondrous things.<br><br>Then it took a boot to my love for female assassins and pushed hard and now I'm sitting at the bottom of a canyon singing to myself:<br><br><i>O' hither she came ,<br>and stole my heart,<br>henceforth I shall never be the same, <br>your jewels to her you will part, <br>or so is the King's claim, <br>a jewelley thief? O' she played it smart,<br>she is of much greater fame,<br>your body she will cart,<br>this deadly daggered dame,<br>your name you will never part,<br>before she takes her aim.</i><br><br>(You're writing it love poetry? Really Mara, REALLY?)<br><br><b>Characters:</b><br>I've already made my adoration towards <b>Celaena</b> quite clear so I'd like to take a moment to appreciate our two leading men: Chaol (still firmly Team Shirtless Chaol) and Dorian (and I wouldn't mind seeing him shirtless too).<br><br><b>Chaol</b>, Chaol, wherefore art thou Chaol? I am, as we speak, arranging to become a fictional character so I can <s>stalk</s> meet you.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681155.gif" width="320" height="195" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Captain of the Guard is as strong and fierce as he was in ToG but in this installment we get to see more of his softer side. The beautiful friendship between Celaena and him takes front stage in CoM. Sarah really takes the opportunity to flesh out their relationship in all it's banter-teasing-tension glory. There's talk of books <i>(sigh)</i> and late nights spent next to the fireplace. <br><br>While Chaol's compassion and loyalty are beacons of light in the darkness of the Royal Court, the question is where exactly do his loyalties lie? With the Crown he has fought so hard to protect? Or with his friends who have made the glass castle a home for him?<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Why are you crying?"<br>"Because," she whispered, her voice shaking, "you remind me of how the world ought to be. What the world <i>can</i> be."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Then there is <b>Dorian</b> our charming prince. But again Sarah sucker punches stereotypes and leaves them panting for breath on the floor. Dorian isn't your garden variety indestructible, white horse riding, fierce, saves-the-day prince. Instead he can be fragile and confused and he is made all the more strong for it. Shocking isn't it that boys can experience the same emotions as female heroines <i>(cough)</i>? Sarah doesn't kick him to the curb either. Rather another layer of mystery is added when strange things start happening to him . . . things that put his life at risk.<br><br>The most refreshing aspect of this trio's relationship is that Celaena is not turned into a Mary Sue mess in the face of these male "interests." Four for you Sarah J. Maas. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681156.gif" width="290" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I am not at all done with these characters and I'm ready for their next adventure. CoM had it all: <b>magic, adventure, epic fights, romance, mystery</b> and <b>secrets</b> . . . so many dirty little secrets that aren't as neatly tucked into the nooks and crannies of the Royal Court as their owners would like to think. The ending left me as hungry for more as when I started. <b>This series is going to go wondrous places in the next instalment and I can barely wait.</b><br><br><br>_____________________________<br><br><b>PRE-REVIEW: 30/09/2012:</b><br><br><i>2013?! No no no no no. Why are you so far away?! <s>2013 is finally here!</s><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681157.gif" width="310" height="155" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just can't. Okay? I need me some more Dorian and Chaol. Pweeeeaaaaase?<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/671107.gif" width="310" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Be strong my shipper heart. Dear lord wilt thou not grant patience to my poor shipper heart?!<br>Team <s>shirtless</s> Chaol.</i><br>  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380226544ra/681158.gif" width="200" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

It brought me right back to the first time I read it and felt my obsession with this series and Sarah J Maas starting! I have fallen in love alllll over again and I'm on such a high right now! 😍😭<br /><br /><br />There’s so much that I just <i>felt!</i><br />Celaena’s character development in this, to her finally beginning to accept and deal with her past, to stop trying to escape what it is she is meant to be, was incredible to read. <br />And it hit me again how much she actually has suffered, from the time she was 8 till now. The people that she has lost, the sacrifices she has made to try and keep her soul intact and completely close herself off to the torture she experienced. It was so painful to read. <br /><br />I’m so not ready and ready for Heir of Fire. Pure pain and excruciating growth resides in that book.</span>
